            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium (Li)-ion batteries (LIB) have governed the current worldwide rechargeable battery market due to their outstanding energy and power capability.  In particular, the LIB's role in enabling elec. vehicles (EVs) has been highlighted to replace the current oil-driven vehicles in order to reduce the usage of oil resources and generation of CO2 gases.  Unlike Li, sodium is one of the more abundant elements on Earth and exhibits similar chem. properties to Li, indicating that Na chem. could be applied to a similar battery system.  In the 1970s-80s, both Na-ion and Li-ion electrodes were investigated, but the higher energy d. of Li-ion cells made them more applicable to small, portable electronic devices, and research efforts for rechargeable batteries have been mainly concd. on LIB since then.  Recently, research interest in Na-ion batteries (NIB) has been resurrected, driven by new applications with requirements different from those in portable electronics, and to address the concern on Li abundance.  In this article, both neg. and pos. electrode materials in NIB are briefly reviewed.  While the voltage is generally lower and the vol. change upon Na removal or insertion is larger for Na-intercalation electrodes, compared to their Li equiv., the power capability can vary depending on the crystal structures.  It is concluded that cost-effective NIB can partially replace LIB, but requires further investigation and improvement.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGonnrfiSUpaRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgEAgLVaSOslw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhtVOrtLjF&amp;md5=485b20393bb8876b2f69ca708aeba606</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.12.012"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhan, J.                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exploring hydrogen molybdenum bronze for sodium ion storage: Performance enhancement by vertical graphene core and conductive polymer shell</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhan, Jiye; Deng, Shengjue; Zhong, Yu; Wang, Yadong; Wang, Xiuli; Yu, Yan; Xia, Xinhui; Tu, Jiangping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">44</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rational construction of high-performance electrode materials is crucial for advancement of sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  In this work, for the first time, we explore the sodium ion storage performance of hydrogen molybdenum bronze (HMB).  To perfect its performance, we controllably sandwich HMB into conductive vertical graphene (VG) skeleton and poly(3,4-ethylenedioxythiophene) shell forming free-standing VG/HMB/PEDOT composite arrays with the help of powerful successive electrodeposition methods.  HMB is completely compatible with VG and PEDOT, and intimately combined with them.  Due to the unique integrated porous structure and omnibearing conductive network, the designed VG/HMB/PEDOT composite arrays show high sodium ion storage capacities (385 mA h g-1 at 200 mA g-1) and superior long-term cycling stability (320 mA h g-1 at 200 mA g-1 after 500 cycles) when used as anode of SIBs, much better than the VG/HMB and HMB/PEDOT counterparts.  Our proposed fabrication strategy offers a new route for designing high-performance electrodes for applications in electrochem. energy storage and electrocatalysis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp3gTLcW8p1kLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhcORke__gV2w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvFyisr7L&amp;md5=e7b1490a2f9bb7dedcb792ee41427ff9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.11.074"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Scalable preparation of porous micron-SnO2/C composites as high performance anode material for lithium ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Ming-Shan; Lei, Ming; Wang, Zhi-Qiang; Zhao, Xing; Xu, Jun; Yang, Wei; Huang, Yun; Li, Xing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">309</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">238-244</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nano tin dioxide-carbon (SnO2/C) composites prepd. by various carbon materials, such as carbon nanotubes, porous carbon, and graphene, have attracted extensive attention in wide fields.  However, undesirable concerns of nanoparticles, including in higher surface area, low tap d., and self-agglomeration, greatly restricted their large-scale practical applications.  In this study, novel porous micron-SnO2/C (p-SnO2/C) composites are scalable prepd. by a simple hydrothermal approach using glucose as a carbon source and Pluronic F127 as a pore forming agent/soft template.  The SnO2 nanoparticles were homogeneously dispersed in micron carbon spheres by assembly with F127/glucose.  The continuous three-dimensional porous carbon networks have effectively provided strain relaxation for SnO2 vol. expansion/shrinkage during lithium insertion/extn.  In addn., the carbon matrix could largely minimize the direct exposure of SnO2 to the electrolyte, thus ensure formation of stable solid electrolyte interface films.  Moreover, the porous structure could also create efficient channels for the fast transport of lithium ions.  As a consequence, the p-SnO2/C composites exhibit stable cycle performance, such as a high capacity retention of over 96% for 100 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1 and a long cycle life up to 800 times at a higher c.d. of 1000 mA g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmFNaEYAc_YbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhcORke__gV2w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xisl2ht7k%253D&amp;md5=92137d91530b423763d2e03cb0556628</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201500097"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reserving Interior Void Space for Volume Change Accommodation: An Example of Cable-Like MWNTs@SnO2@C Composite for Superior Lithium and Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao Yi; Wei Chao; Sun Shengnan; Wang Luyuan Paul; Xu Zhichuan J</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Reserving interior void space in the cable-like structure of multiwalled carbon nanotubes-in-SnO2-in-carbon layer (MWNTs@SnO2@C) is reported for the first time.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Confined annealing-induced transformation of tin oxide into sulfide for sodium storage applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Xuming; Xiao, Fengping; Wang, Shuo; Liu, Jin; Leung, Michael K. H.; Yu, Denis Y. W.; Rogach, Andrey L.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">As conversion-type anode materials for Na ion batteries, metal sulfides have a lower theor. capacity but generally deliver a much higher reversible capacity in practice than their oxide counterparts.  The origin of this phenomenon was not fundamentally understood yet.  From a reaction enthalpy anal., the authors reveal that the sulfidation reaction with S is possible for a wide variety of metal oxides.  The authors proceeded to convert the less anode-active Sn oxide/C (SnO2/C) composites into the highly anode-active Sn sulfide/C (SnS2/C) materials by confined annealing with S powder.  For anode applications in Na ion batteries, SnS2/C delivers a reversible capacity of 770 mA h g-1, which is more than double the value of SnO2/C (360 mA h g-1).  The obsd. superiority of SnS2/C anodes is correlated with the narrower band gap, higher conversion potential that allows for a larger polarization, and more energetically favorable conversion process on the surface of SnS2.  In particular, the authors demonstrate a modeling strategy for surface conversion reactions, which could potentially be considered for the kinetics study of various conversion-type anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6tVVHSnBOArVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhcORke__gV2w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXotFWqu78%253D&amp;md5=aa76c6447317d89e9d9edee11e15f64a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1039/C3TA13592F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrafine SnO2 nanoparticle loading onto reduced graphene oxide as anodes for sodium-ion batteries with superior rate and cycling performances</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yun-Xiao; Lim, Young-Geun; Park, Min-Sik; Chou, Shu-Lei; Kim, Jung Ho; Liu, Hua-Kun; Dou, Shi-Xue; Kim, Young-Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A structured SnO2-reduced graphene oxide (RGO) nanocomposite has been synthesized with SnO2 nanoparticles (∼5 nm) anchored on a RGO framework.  It has been successfully applied as an anode material in sodium-ion batteries.  The electrode delivers a reversible Na-storage capacity of 330 mA.h.g-1 with an outstanding capacity retention of 81.3% over 150 cycles.  Moreover, it possesses a relatively good rate capability, exhibiting a capacity retention of 25.8% at high rate (1000 mA.h.g-1).                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-dimensional porous graphene-encapsulated CNT@SnO2 composite for high-performance lithium and sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Dan; Li, Xiaogang; Fan, Li-Zhen; Deng, Yonghong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">230</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sn oxide (SnO2) is regarded as a promising anode material for both Li-ion batteries (LIBs) and Na-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its large theor. capacity.  However, poor elec. cond. and the weak cyclability resulted from dramatic vol. expansion upon cycling process still hinder its practical application.  Herein, the authors report a facile two-step hydrothermal route to encapsulate core-shell structured C nanotube (CNT)@SnO2 composite in a graphene coating with novel three-dimensional (3D) porous framework architecture (CNT@SnO2@G) as anode for both LIBs and SIBs.  The resultant CNT@SnO2@G electrode suggests outstanding Li and Na storage performance with large specific capacity, remarkable cycling stability and excellent rate capability.  For LIBs, it delivers a high initial discharge capacity of 1400 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, improved reversible capacity of 947 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1, and enhanced rate capability of 281 mAh g-1 at 3000 mA g-1.  Na storage testing suggests that a high discharge capacity of 323 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 25 mA g-1 was achieved.  The present unique structural design assocd. with the remarkable Li and Na storage performance ensures CNT@SnO2@G as an advanced anode material for rechargeable LIBs and SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpYjZeo89itC7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljp6H2s54YcpA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXitlOqsrg%253D&amp;md5=cd2a7d386059a603884dc4097ec6f4eb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA06080J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yue, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, W.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Triple-walled SnO2@N-doped carbon@SnO2 nanotubes as an advanced anode material for lithium and sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yue, Jie; Wang, Wenpeng; Wang, Nana; Yang, Xianfeng; Feng, Jinkui; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Triple-walled SnO2@N-doped C@SnO2 nanotubes are synthesized by a facile process with high-quality PPy nanotubes as the template.  This structure has SnO2 nanoparticles closely attached to both the external and internal surfaces of N-doped C nanotubes, thus assuring good charge-transfer kinetics to all the SnO2 nanoparticles.  Meanwhile, it doubles the loading d. of SnO2 in the nanocomposite, and offers adequate room to accommodate the vol. deformation of SnO2 on/in the nanotubes.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Simple synthesis of hollow tin dioxide microspheres and their application to lithium-ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Sangjin; Jang, Byungchul; Kim, Taeahn; Oh, Seung M.; Hyeon, Taeghwan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow Sn dioxide (SnO2) microspheres were synthesized by heat treatment of a mixt. of Sn(IV) tetrachloride pentahydrate (SnCl4·5H2O) and resorcinol-formaldehyde gel (RF gel).  Because hollow structures form during the heat treatment, the pre-formation of a template and the adsorption of a target precursor on the template is unnecessary in this method, leading to simplified synthetic procedures and facilitating mass prodn.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors successfully synthesized large-scale and highly pure ultrathin SnO2 nanosheets (NSs), with a min. thickness in the regime of ∼2.1 nm as detd. by HRTEM and in good agreement with XRD refinements and AFM height profiles.  Through TEM and HRTEM observations on time-dependent samples, the as-prepd. SnO2 NSs were assembled by oriented attachment of preformed SnO2 nanoparticles (NPs).  Systematic trials showed that well-defined ultrathin SnO2 NSs could only be obtained under appropriate reaction time, solvent, additive, precursor concn., and cooling rate.  A certain degree of nonstoichiometry appears inevitable in the well-defined SnO2 NSs sample.  However, deviations from the optimal synthetic parameters give rise to severe nonstoichiometry in the products, giving Sn3O4 or SnO.  This finding may open new accesses to the fundamental studies of Sn oxides as well as their intertransition processes.  Finally, the authors studied the Li-ion storage of the SnO2 NSs as compared to SnO2 hollow spheres and NPs.  The results showed superior performance of SnO2 NSs sample over its two counterparts.  This greatly enhanced Li-ion storage capability of SnO2 NSs is probably resulting from the ultrathin thicknesses and the unique porous structures: the nanometer-sized networks provide negligible diffusion times of ions thus faster phase transitions, while the breathable interior porous structure can effectively buffer the drastic vol. changes during lithiation and delithiation reactions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr_qllqur3xdLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgc59buflCy7Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XosFCiuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=a7c4eacc446a30499588ac7c89a8c886</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1021/ja909321d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, M. These results indicate that the coating of reduced graphene oxide is an effective strategy to buffer vol. change and improve charge transfer resistance during Na+ ion insertion/extn. for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrB445H1Muj07Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgc59buflCy7Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXltlyqtbs%253D&amp;md5=73ed80748af6f2a43fc595a5190dde04</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA05390A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Amorphous Tin-Based Nanohybrid for Ultra-Stable Sodium Storage</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An amorphous tin-based nanohybrid for ultra-stable sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhongtao; Feng, Jianze; Hu, Han; Dong, Yunfa; Ren, Hao; Wu, Wenting; Hu, Zhenpeng; Wu, Mingbo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The natural abundance of sodium resources makes sodium-ion batteries a potential and promising alternative to lithium ion battery technol. for large-scale energy storage application.  However, the long-term stability of sodium ion batteries is largely hindered by the widely employed cryst. electrode materials, for example tin-based compds., because of their structural degrdn. and pulverization during cycling.  Herein, an ultra-stable sodium ion battery anode material by rationally manipulating a cryst. tin-based compd. into an amorphous structure is reported for the first time.  Typically, a phosphorus-contg. monomer is polymd. on tin oxide quantum dots dispersed on graphene oxide nanosheets, further mediating the formation of a stable and amorphous tin-based hybrid at elevated temps.  The robust cyclability and structural stability are well demonstrated by performance evaluation and ex situ characterization.  The unique structural design proposed here may open up new avenues for developing advanced metal oxide anode materials for sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo5zKZckPvCO7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgc59buflCy7Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhsVOnur3E&amp;md5=fcf4693df01a7ef15a14cb4ebc73fda1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b06230"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Diemant, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Geiger, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Raccichini, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Behm, R.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrafast Ionic Liquid-Assisted Microwave Synthesis of SnO Microflowers and Their Superior Sodium-Ion Storage Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qin, Bingsheng; Zhang, Huang; Diemant, Thomas; Geiger, Dorin; Raccichini, Rinaldo; Behm, R.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin oxide (SnO) is considered one of the most promising metal oxides for utilization as anode material in sodium ion batteries (SIBs), because of its ease of synthesis, high specific gravimetric capacity, and satisfactory cycling performance.  However, to aim at practical applications, the Coulombic efficiency during cycling needs to be further improved, which requires a deeper knowledge of its working mechanism.  Here, a microflower-shaped SnO material is synthesized by means of an ultrafast ionic liq.-assisted microwave method.  The as-prepd. SnO anode active material exhibits excellent cycling performance, good Coulombic efficiency as well as a large capacity delivered at low potential, which is fundamental to maximize the energy output of SIBs.  These overall merits were never reported before for pure SnO anodes (i.e., not in a composite with, for example, graphene).  Addnl., by combining ex situ XRD and XPS, it is clearly demonstrated for the first time that the Sn-Na alloy, which is formed during the initial sodium sodiation, desodiates in two successive but fully sepd. steps.  Totally different from the previous report, the pristine SnO phase is not regenerated upon desodiation up to 3 V vs Na/Na+.  The newly disclosed reaction route provides an alternative view of the complex reaction mechanism of these families of metal oxides for sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpoyJ3FH4dtL7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljicEbClOS7sQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXht1Sjt7bO&amp;md5=1ce9f539539ae7ac5d490485ee0ae1be</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201300105"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, H.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Smart Construction of Integrated CNTs/Li4Ti5O12 Core/Shell Arrays with Superior High-Rate Performance for Application in Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yao Zhujun; Xia Xinhui; Zhou Cheng-Ao; Zhong Yu; Deng Shengjue; Wang Weiqi; Wang Xiuli; Tu Jiangping; Wang Yadong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Exploring advanced high-rate anodes is of great importance for the development of next-generation high-power lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  Here, novel carbon nanotubes (CNTs)/Li4Ti5O12 (LTO) core/shell arrays on carbon cloth (CC) as integrated high-quality anode are constructed via a facile combined chemical vapor deposition-atomic layer deposition (ALD) method.  ALD-synthesized LTO is strongly anchored on the CNTs' skeleton forming core/shell structures with diameters of 70-80 nm the combined advantages including highly conductive network, large surface area, and strong adhesion are obtained in the CC-LTO@CNTs core/shell arrays.  The electrochemical performance of the CC-CNTs/LTO electrode is completely studied as the anode of LIBs and it shows noticeable high-rate capability (a capacity of 169 mA h g(-1) at 1 C and 112 mA h g(-1) at 20 C), as well as a stable cycle life with a capacity retention of 86% after 5000 cycles at 10 C, which is much better than the CC-LTO counterpart.  Meanwhile, excellent cycling stability is also demonstrated for the full cell with LiFePO4 cathode and CC-CNTs/LTO anode (87% capacity retention after 1500 cycles at 10 C).         </div><div class="casAbstract">The com. advancement of high-performance sodium ion batteries is highly dependent on the judicious design/construction of advanced electrode materials.  In this work, we construct novel P2-type Na0.7MnO2.05 nanotube/carbon nanotube (NMO/CNT) core/branch composites via a powerful three-step process for sodium ion battery (SIB) applications.  P2-type Na0.7MnO2.05 nanotubes of about 500 nm have been, for the first time to our knowledge, fabricated and further modified by cocoon-like CNT branches.  The cycling performance is increased significantly with an encouraging capacity retention of 88% at 0.1 A g-1 after 100 cycles due to enhanced electrochem. kinetics and improved structural stabilization resulting from the CNT cocoon branches.  To assess the practical functionality as a full cell, a helical carbon nanofiber (HCNF) anode with capacitive-dominated sodium ion storage is also developed to match with the NMO/CNT cathode.  The new-type NMO/CNT//HCNF full cells exhibit encouraging cycle performance with a capacity retention of 71% after 200 cycles at 100 mA g-1 and superior rate performance to the unmodified NMO//HCNF full cells.  Our electrode design strategy provides a new way for fabricating high-performance electrode materials for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsj7qSeyxUW7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljicEbClOS7sQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVynt7%252FJ&amp;md5=1101720455f50e45ba49886ea11871aa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.ceramint.2005.11.013"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Seo, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Akutsu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kagemoto, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Preparation and Properties of Sb-Doped SnO<sub>2</sub>/Metal Substrates by Sol–gel and Dip Coating</span>. <i>Ceram. When the SnO2@PANI composite was used as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) it exhibited a long cycle life and good rate capability.  The SnO2@PANI composite is able to deliver a relatively high reversible capacity of 213.5 mA h g-1 after 400 cycles at 300 mA g-1, while a bare SnO2 particle anode can only deliver a considerably lower capacity of 14.4 mA h g-1 after 400 cycles at the same c.d.  The enhanced electrochem. performance could be ascribed to the unique hollow structure and the PANI buffer layer, which are found to be beneficial in decreasing the likelihood of the pulverization of SnO2 and agglomeration of the generated Sn particles during the discharge and charge process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoUvWAfADU9FrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljA-HAJbPH-JA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksF2qsLw%253D&amp;md5=dc8efb164f66c0eb8a7e6684fc378f62</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201800610"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, J.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Freeze-Drying-Assisted Synthesis of Porous SnO2/rGO Xerogels as Anode Materials for Highly Reversible Lithium/Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Chao; Jiang, Jialin; Xu, Tingting; Ji, Hongmei; Yang, Yang; Yang, Gang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Three-dimensional porous SnO2/rGO xerogels with superior cycling performance in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are fabricated through a freeze-drying-assisted method.  SnO2 nanoparticles (5 nm in diam.) are homogeneously attached to the surface of graphene sheets without self-aggregation.  The heterostructured SnO2/rGO xerogel possesses numerous micron-sized pores that can efficiently buffer the volumetric change of SnO2 during the charge/discharge process and provide multidimensional channels, improving the cond. between active materials and electrolyte.  The SnO2/rGO xerogel exhibits excellent electrochem. performance, both in LIBs and SIBs, owing to its particular porous structure.  For LIBs, it delivers a high initial discharge capacity of 1670.5 mAh g-1 in the first cycle and remains at 1139.4 mAh g-1 after 166 cycles at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1.  The SnO2/rGO xerogel also delivers a high discharge capacity of 189.4 mAh g-1 without capacity loss over 266 cycles at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1 for SIBs.  The SnO2/rGO xerogel can be used as an electrode material in both LIBs and SIBs, and can maintain an excellent rate performance and cyclic performance, owing to the abundant porosity and high cond.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpo0taOWd07nrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljA-HAJbPH-JA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtFGkt7vO&amp;md5=3645302d42e933025e897c710d782332</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201601804"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, X.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen and oxygen co-doping carbon microspheres by a sustainable route for fast sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Fang; Qin, Decai; Xu, Jiaxin; Liu, Zhanying; Zhao, Yanzhang; Zhang, Xiaogang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Heteroatom-doping was regarded as an effective strategy to regulate the Na storage performance of C materials.  N and O dual-doped C microspheres (NO-CS) from the rinds of corn stalks were fabricated via a tailored carbonization and soln. doping route.  NO-CS reveals both high O (15.6 at.%), N (6.4 at.%) contents and high sp. surface area (746.48 m2 g-1).  The NO-CS derived C anode shows tremendous reversible capacity, rate capability and cycling stability, e.g. 270 mAh g-1 over 200 cycles at 50 mA g-1, 130 mAh g-1 over 3500 cycles at 5 A g-1.  The superior Na storage property may due to the abundant porosity and dual-doping that boost fast ion adsorption at the graphene layer defects and N O moiety of C.  Scalable and cost-effective synthesis route with outstanding Na storage performance makes NO-CS a competitive anode material for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrT44xGA_DW37Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCUAxokQXj9g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXjs1Sru7k%253D&amp;md5=5e128a972eb9c3df7501988663c2193f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.jelechem.2018.11.056"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nitrogen-Doping of Graphene Enhancing Sodium Storage of SnO<sub>2</sub> Anode</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-doping of graphene enhancing sodium storage of SnO2 anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fan, Linlin; Song, Xiaosheng; Xiong, Dongbin; Li, Xifei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Electroanalytical Chemistry</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Currently, challenges are still pervasive in developing excellent new materials for Na-ion batteries (SIBs).  The authors design SnO2/N-doped graphene (SnO2/NG) composites for SIBs.  The SnO2/NG anodes with the optimal N-doping level exhibit enhanced reversible capacities and rate capabilities over undoped anodes.  More importantly, the pyridinic-N is the main contributor to excellent cycling capacity of SnO2/NG.  Consequently, the resultant SnO2/NG composite with higher content of pyridinic-N (1.97%) delivers outstanding reversible capacity of 409.6 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 when the cycling nos. increase to 100 cycles, and it also presents superior rate capabilities of 416.5, 366.9, and 318.7 mAh g-1 at 200, 400, and 800 mA g-1, resp.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synergistic effect induced ultrafine SnO2/graphene nanocomposite as an advanced lithium/sodium-ion batteries anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Weihua; Song, Keming; Mi, Liwei; Feng, Xiangming; Zhang, Jianmin; Cui, Shizhong; Liu, Chuntai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnO2/graphene materials have received extensive attention in broad applications owning to their excellent performances.  However, multi-step and harsh synthetic methods with high temps. and high pressures are major obstacles that need to be overcome.  Herein a simple, low-cost, and scalable approach is proposed to construct ultrafine SnO2/graphene nanomaterials effectively under const. pressure and at the low temp. of 80 °C for 4 h, in which ultrafine SnO2 nanoparticles grow on graphene sheets uniformly and firmly via Sn-O-C bonding.  This result depends on the synergetic effect of two reactions, the redn. of graphene oxide and formation of SnO2 nanoparticles, which are achieved successfully.  More importantly, the constructed SnO2/graphene material exhibits excellent electrochem. properties in both lithium-ion batteries and sodium-ion batteries.  As an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, it displays a high reversible capacity (1420 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 after 90 cycles) and good cycling life (97% at 1 A g-1 after 230 cycles), whereas in sodium-ion batteries, it maintains a capacity of 1280 mA h g-1 at 0.05 A g-1 and 650 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 after 90 cycles.  The proposed synthetic methodol. paves the way for the effective and large scale prepn. of graphene-based composites for broad applications such as energy storage, optoelectronic devices, and catalysis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoI5M6-NJwBYLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCUAxokQXj9g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXmslWrs70%253D&amp;md5=c8b03b5c9de2e24ea880cb3e5885057f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-017-1756-3"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, J.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Multifunctional SnO2/3D graphene hybrid materials for sodium-ion and lithium-ion batteries with excellent rate capability and long cycle life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Jung-In; Song, Junhua; Cha, Younghwan; Fu, Shaofang; Zhu, Chengzhou; Li, Xiaolin; Lin, Yuehe; Song, Min-Kyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4398-4414</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnO2 is a promising material for both Li-ion and Na-ion batteries owing to its high theor. capacities.  Unfortunately, the electrochem. performance of SnO2 is unsatisfactory because of the large vol. change that occurs during cycling, low electronic cond. of inactive oxide matrix, and poor kinetics, which are particularly severe in Na-ion batteries.  Herein, ultra-fine SnO2 nanocrystals anchored on a unique three-dimensional (3D) porous reduced graphene oxide (rGO) matrix are described as promising bifunctional electrodes for Li-ion and Na-ion batteries with excellent rate capability and long cycle life.  Ultra-fine SnO2 nanocrystals of size ∼6 nm are well-coordinated to the graphene sheets that comprise the 3D macro-porous structure.  Notably, superior rate capability was obtained up to 3 C (1/n C is a measure of the rate that allows the cell to be charged/discharged in n h) for both batteries.  In situ X-ray diffractometry measurements during lithiation (or sodiation) and delithiation (or desodiation) were combined with various electrochem. techniques to reveal the real-time phase evolution.  This crit. information was linked with the internal resistance, ion diffusivity (DLi+ and DNa+), and the unique structure of the composite electrode materials to explain their excellent electrochem. performance.  The improved capacity and superior rate capabilities demonstrated in this work can be ascribed to the enhanced transport kinetics of both electrons and ions within the electrode structure because of the well-interconnected, 3D macro-porous rGO matrix.  The porous rGO matrix appears to play a more important role in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), where the larger mass/radius of Na-ions are marked concerns.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqidfVgimZOI7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCUAxokQXj9g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsVGksbjI&amp;md5=83af205a83c8bc1959d522415686bb4a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201702225"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Y.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mesoporous Tin-Based Oxide Nanospheres/Reduced Graphene Composites as Advanced Anodes for Lithium-Ion Half/Full Cells and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Yanyan; Li, Aihua; Dong, Caifu; Li, Chuanchuan; Xu, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The large vol. variations of tin-based oxides hinder their extensive application in the field of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  In this study, structure design, hybrid fabrication, and carbon-coating approaches have been simultaneously adopted to address these shortcomings.  To this end, uniform mesoporous NiO/SnO2@rGO, Ni-Sn oxide@rGO, and SnO2@rGO nanosphere composites have been selectively fabricated.  Among them, the obtained NiO/SnO2@rGO composite exhibited a high capacity of 800 mAh g-1 at 1000 mA g-1 after 400 cycles.  The electrochem. mechanism of NiO/SnO2 as an anode for LIBs has been preliminarily investigated by ex situ XRD pattern anal.  Furthermore, an NiO/SnO2@rGO-LiCoO2 lithium-ion full cell showed a high capacity of 467.8 mAh g-1 at 500 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  Notably, the NiO/SnO2@rGO composite also showed good performance when investigated as an anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  It is believed that the unique mesoporous nanospherical framework, synergistic effects between the various components, and uniform rGO wrapping of NiO/SnO2 shorten the Li+ ion diffusion pathways, maintain sufficient contact between the active material and the electrolyte, mitigate vol. changes, and finally improve the elec. cond. of the electrode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpijGd4NTLVw7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCUAxokQXj9g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsVekur7P&amp;md5=f28f0582025d603cb6405eafd3bea208</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1007/s10570-016-0966-2"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dursun, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sar, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ata, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Morcrette, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Akbas, M.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">SnO2 Nanosheets Anchored on a 3D, Bicontinuous Electron and Ion Transport Carbon Network for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Xun; Luo, Ming; Zhao, Wenxia; Xu, Ruimei; Liu, Yong; Shen, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We demonstrate the in situ growth of SnO2 nanosheets on a freestanding carbonized eggshell membrane (CEM), which provides three-dimensional, bicontinuous electron and ion transport pathways through a massively interconnected C fiber skeleton and interpenetrated pore network, resp. When used as an additive-free anode in a Na-ion battery, SnO2 nanosheets can realize a complete electrochem. reaction and maintain good cycling stability with the help of a CEM.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Poly(3,4-ethylenedioxythiophene) sheath over a SnO2 hollow spheres/graphene oxide hybrid for a durable anode in Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bhaskar, Akkisetty; Deepa, Melepurath; Ramakrishna, M.; Rao, T. N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">118</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7296-7306</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnO2 hollow spheres (HSs) were synthesized by a hydrothermal route by use of an org. additive (2-mercaptopropionic acid or MPA) and a cationic surfactant (cetyltrimethyl ammonium bromide or CTAB).  The progressive transformation of SnO2 solid spheres to SnO2 HSs 140-150 nm in dimensions wherein a thin shell of densely packed SnO2 crystallites with a tetragonal crystal structure surrounds an empty core was followed by scanning- and transmission-electron microscopy.  The roles of MPA as the HS structure-directing agent, CTAB as the moiety which prevents HS aggregation, and water as the solvent crucial for hollow core formation were independently detd. by elaborate morphol. analyses.  With the goal of realizing superior electrochem. performance, hybrids of optimized SnO2 HSs embedded in graphene oxide (GO) nanosheets and enveloped by a sheath of a conducting polymer, poly(3,4-ethylenedioxythiophene) or PEDOT, were also synthesized; the continuity of the amorphous PEDOT coating on SnO2 HS/GO was confirmed by elemental mapping and XPS.  Galvanostatic charge-discharge studies revealed an initial reversible capacity of 990 mA h g-1 for SnO2 HSs at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, and a capacity of 400 mA h g-1 was retained after 30 cycles.  A significant improvement in cycling performance was achieved in the SnO2 HS/GO/PEDOT hybrid, as the synergy between the moderately high intrinsic electronic cond. of GO nanosheets and the ability of PEDOT to buffer the vol. change during repetitive Li+ charge-discharge more efficiently compared to pristine SnO2 HS impart a capacity of 608 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 to the hybrid, retained at the end of 150 cycles, and the latter value was ∼1248 mA h g-1 when the mass of only the SnO2 HS in the hybrid was considered.  The SnO2 HS/GO/PEDOT hybrid also showed an excellent rate capability as a capacity of 381 mA h g-1 was attained even at a high c.d. of 2000 mA g-1.  We demonstrate the viability of the SnO2 HS/GO/PEDOT hybrid as a durable high performance anode for Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGot6gQBx-SerrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhba_sLo9nWpQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXksVWjtrc%253D&amp;md5=2c8b2f650affc6e682e7aee013398764</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.01.158"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Z.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of three-dimensional hollow SnO2@PPy nanotube arrays via template-assisted method and chemical vapor-phase polymerization as high performance anodes for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Zhenzhen; Yang, Hongyan; Dou, Peng; Wang, Chao; Zheng, Jiao; Xu, Xinhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">209</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel polypyrrole (PPy) coated three-dimensional (3D) SnO2 nanotube arrays (SnO2@PPy) was synthesized via a template-assisted method followed by a chem. vapor-phase polymn. process as a high performance anode for Li-ion batteries.  In this new type electrode material, the hollow interiors of SnO2 are able to provide enough spaces for the accommodation of large vol. expansion during the insertion of Li-ion, making for the improvement of the stability of electrode.  Meanwhile, the addn. of conductive PPy layer could facilitate the electron transport, prevent the aggregation of active materials and warrant the stability of as-formed solid electrolyte interface (SEI) films.  As a result, the integration of 3-dimensional hybrid nanostructure electrode is capable of retaining a high capacity of 646 mA h g-1 after 150 cycles with a coulomb efficiency &gt;98% and a capacity retention of 221 mA h g-1 even at a high c.d. of 5000 mA g-1, revealing better cycling and rate properties compared with bare SnO2 nanotube arrays anode.  This nanoengineering strategy can provide a facile and controllable way to synthesize other anode materials for Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr26Yy9rTzS87Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhba_sLo9nWpQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XptVGhurc%253D&amp;md5=fcafa7e40960e668e75ff5301dfafa36</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.elecom.2016.09.012"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Heterogeneous branched core-shell SnO2-PANI nanorod arrays with mechanical integrity and three dimentional electron transport for lithium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Wangwang; Zhao, Kangning; Niu, Chaojiang; Zhang, Lei; Cai, Zhengyang; Han, Chunhua; He, Liang; Shen, Teng; Yan, Mengyu; Qu, Longbing; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnO2 with high theor. capacity has long suffered from its instinct large vol. variation and low elec. transport linked to poor cycling stability and rate performance.  Here we present the heterogeneous branched core-shell SnO2-PANI nanorod arrays which have been successfully designed and fabricated by an efficient and facile hydrothermal treatment followed by electrodeposition.  The heterogeneous core-shell SnO2-PANI nanorod arrays exhibit a high reversible capacity of 506 mAh/g after 100 cycles, resulting the capacity fading of 0.579% per cycle between 20 and 100 cycles, much lower than that of nanosheet-assembled hierarchal SnO2-PANI nanorod arrays (1.150%) and bare SnO2 nanorod arrays (1.151%).  At high c.d. of 3000 mA/g, heterogeneous core-shell SnO2-PANI nanorod arrays maintain a capacity of 660 mAh/g after the c.d. returns to 100 mA/g, 3 times as high as that of nanosheet-assembled hierarchal SnO2-PANI nanorod arrays (206 mAh/g) and 6 times as high as that of bare SnO2 nanorod (124 mAh/g).  The enhanced electrochem. performance can be attributed to the branched conductive PANI shells, which not only release the stress of vol. expansion and maintain mech. integrity during cycling, but also realize three dimensional transport for electrons.  Our work demonstrates a great potential for the application of heterogeneous branched core-shell PANI-SnO2 nanorod arrays for lithium batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqPB49HkBb6ybVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhba_sLo9nWpQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtlOmtL3N&amp;md5=42690cb95f09b24fd072a2321173da47</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201810729"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The design and synthesis of hierarchical microboxes, assembled from SnS nanoplates coated with nitrogen-doped carbon (NC) as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries, is demonstrated.  The template-engaged multistep synthesis of the SnS@NC microboxes involves sequential phase transformation, polydopamine coating, and thermal annealing in N2.  The SnS@NC composite with two-dimensional nano-sized subunits rationally integrates several advantages including shortening the diffusion path of electrons/Na+ ions, improving elec. cond., and alleviating vol. variation of the electrode material. The resulting 3D lamellar SnO2/CC can be directly used as an electrode in supercapacitors without the necessity for addn. of either binder or conductive species, and achieves a specific capacitance as high as 247 F g-1 at a c.d. of 1 A g-1 within a potential window ranging from -0.6 to 0.3 V because of the unique porous structure accessible to electrolyte ions. The device exhibits not only an excellent cycle stability (76.9% after 10 000 cycles at 3 A g-1), but also high energy d. of 22.8 W h kg-1 at a power d. of 850 W kg-1 under a cell voltage of 1.7 V.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Polypyrrole (PPy) was synthesized by chem. oxidative polymn. technique using monomer pyrrole and ammonium persulfate as an oxidant in a ratio of 1:1.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding and controlling the substrate effect on graphene electron-transfer chemistry via reactivity imprint lithography</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qing Hua; Jin, Zhong; Kim, Ki Kang; Hilmer, Andrew J.; Paulus, Geraldine L.         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene has exceptional electronic, optical, mech. and thermal properties, which provide it with great potential for use in electronic, optoelectronic and sensing applications.  The chem. functionalization of graphene was studied with a view to controlling its electronic properties and interactions with other materials.  Covalent modification of graphene by org. diazonium salts was used to achieve these goals, but because graphene comprises only a single at. layer, it is strongly influenced by the underlying substrate.  Here, the authors show a Stark difference in the rate of electron-transfer reactions with org. diazonium salts for monolayer graphene supported on a variety of substrates.  Reactions proceed rapidly for graphene supported on SiO2 and Al2O3 (sapphire), but negligibly on alkyl-terminated and hexagonal boron nitride (hBN) surfaces, as shown by Raman spectroscopy.  The authors also develop a model of reactivity based on substrate-induced electron-hole puddles in graphene, and achieve spatial patterning of chem. reactions in graphene by patterning the substrate.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQYXd7YFJl3bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljR6LvLdpltWQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhtFOgtrbM&amp;md5=9cae91dfb1930855e06a54d1df3396ed</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1039/c2an36059d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Microwave-assisted synthesis of carbon nanodots through an eggshell membrane and their fluorescent application</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qi; Liu, Xing; Zhang, Lichun; Lv, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Analyst (Cambridge, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">137</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5392-5397</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon nanodots (C-Dots) as a new form of carbonaceous nanomaterials have aroused much interest and intensive research due to their inspiring properties.  Compared to traditional semiconductor quantum dots, these newly emergent nanodots possess a no. of advantageous characteristics, among which low-toxicity is particularly fascinating.  More and more research into C-Dots have focused on synthesis methods and biol.-related applications.  Microwave-assisted approaches have attracted attention because microwave treatment can provide intensive and efficient energy, and as a consequence shorten the reaction time.  The authors designed a "green", rapid, eco-friendly and waste-reused approach to synthesize fluorescent and water-sol. C-Dots from eggshell membrane (ESM) ashes according to a microwave-assisted process.  ESM selected as the carbon source was a common protein-rich waste in daily life and can be obtained easily and cheaply.  The C-Dots from the authors' method showed the maximal fluorescence emission peak at 450 nm and the fluorescence quantum yield was ∼14%.  The authors further designed a sensitive probe for glutathione based on the fluorescence turn off and on of the C-Dots-Cu2+ system, which showed a linear range of 0.5-80 μmol L-1 and detection limit of 0.48 μmol L-1.  In general, the C-Dots prepd. briefly and inexpensively from ESM revealed excellent fluorescent property with promising potential for applications such as sample detection and biotechnol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoInLlDDE8hZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljR6LvLdpltWQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsFSqs7jN&amp;md5=c37d103945c62373ee56a6ff1c2e984e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1039/c2nr33482h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanosize SnO2 confined in the porous shells of carbon cages for kinetically efficient and long-term lithium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Guangmin; Wang, Da-Wei; Li, Lu; Li, Na; Li, Feng; Cheng, Hui-Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1576-1582</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We explore a hybrid material consisting of SnO2 nanoparticles (NPs) embedded in the porous shells of carbon cages (SnO2-PSCC).  The hybrid material exhibits improved kinetics of lithiation-delithiation and high reversible capacity, and excellent cyclic stability without capacity loss over 100 cycles at 500 mA g-1 with a coulombic efficiency close to 100% after the initial cycle.  This can be ascribed to the high elec. cond., the hierarchical porosity and the confinement effect of the PSCC on the vol. change of SnO2 NPs.  The material has a large reversible capacity of 460 mA h g-1 at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1 due to a short ion diffusion length in the bulk and large no. of inter-pore ion transport channels.  These results provide insight into improving the lithium storage performance of SnO2 by facilitating the reaction kinetics and indicate that this hybrid material has great potential for use in high-rate and durable lithium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsZT4u5tswSrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljR6LvLdpltWQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFGlurc%253D&amp;md5=3cc7762bfa04437dac732448002d4444</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b08901"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ruan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible Overoxidized Polypyrrole Films with Orderly Structure as High-Performance Anodes for Li- and Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yuan, Tao; Ruan, Jiafeng; Zhang, Weimin; Tan, Zhuopeng; Yang, Junhe; Ma, Zi-Feng; Zheng, Shiyou</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">35114-35122</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Flexible polypyrrole (PPy) films with highly ordered structures were fabricated by a novel vapor phase polymn. (VPP) process and used as the anode material in Li-ion batteries (LIBs) and Na-ion batteries (SIBs).  The PPy films demonstrate excellent rate performance and cycling stability.  At a charge/discharge rate of 1 C, the reversible capacities of the PPy film anode reach 284.9 and 177.4 mAh/g in LIBs and SIBs, resp.  Even at a charge/discharge rate of 20 C, the reversible capacity of the PPy film anode retains 54.0 and 52.9% of the capacity of 1 C in LIBs and SIBs, resp.  After 1000 electrochem. cycles at a rate of 10 C, there is no obvious capacity fading.  The mol. structure and electrochem. behaviors of Li- and Na-ion doping and dedoping in the PPy films are studied by XPS and ex situ XRD.  It is believed that the PPy film electrodes in the overoxidized state can be reversibly charged and discharged through the doping and dedoping of Li or Na ions.  Because of the self-adaptation of the doped ions, the ordered pyrrolic chain structure can realize a fast charge/discharge process.  This result may substantially contribute to the progress of research into flexible polymer electrodes in various types of batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo-CXU7OX5Yq7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljETPjGZBjXKQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitVSrsbjI&amp;md5=9d548f514f3b364ed646cf02862b4567</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta01515g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vinayan, B.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of SnO2 nanoparticles dispersed nitrogen doped graphene anode material for ultrahigh capacity lithium ion battery applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Vinayan, B.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors report a facile strategy to synthesize SnO2 nanoparticles dispersed N doped graphene (SnO2/NG).  N doping of graphene was carried out by the pyrolysis of polypyrrole coated poly(sodium 4-styrenesulfonate) functionalized graphene.  The SnO2 nanoparticles are dispersed over N doped graphene by a modified polyol redn. method.  The dispersed SnO2 nanoparticles are 2-3 nm in size with homogeneous dispersion and good crystallinity.  The SnO2/NG as an anode material in Li ion batteries displays superior reversible capacity, very good rate capability and excellent cyclic performance (1220 mA h g-1 after 100th cycle).  The impedance measurements show that N doping can significantly reduce the charge transfer resistance of graphene based electrodes.  The factors contributing to the excellent electrochem. performance of the SnO2/NG anode material is discussed.  The present work opens a new pathway for the development of metal or metal oxide nanoparticle-N doped C nanostructure based nanocomposites for high performance electrochem. energy devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrTwY9D4k-NZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljETPjGZBjXKQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXjtlWqsb8%253D&amp;md5=69cb0036ea483ea3ba70d7fed606fc47</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1016/j.elecom.2011.09.014"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, Q.         </div><div class="casAbstract">SnO2-based composite coaxial nanocables with multi-walled carbon nanotube (MWCNT) and polypyrrole (PPy), SnO2@MWCNT@SnO2@PPy were successfully synthesized via a simple one-pot chem. route.
